Rebbi Jehudah permits, but according to Rav Hisda he only permits what on the Sabbath would not be a clear completion of one of the 39 forbidden kinds of work. He permits sharpening the tip, not making a tip which would turn a stick into a spit and therefore violate “hitting with hammer”.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanania the son of Rebbi Abbahu said, to make fire from wood is between them<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Starting a new fire on firewood is clearly a complete action forbidden on the Sabbath, and in his opinion permitted by R. Jehudah.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah bar Pazi stated from Bar Delaiah: what is the matter<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">He quotes a Tanna who confesses his inability to decide between Rav Ḥisda and R. Abbahu’s son.</i>? Is the matter to sharpen the tip of the spit? or is the matter to make fire from the stones? You only have the following<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">Quoted from Chapter 3, Halakhah 8.</i>: “One does not sharpen the knife but he cleanses it on another.” Rav Ḥisda said, this is Rebbi Jehudah’s. Rav Jehudah in the name of Samuel said, it is everybody’s opinion, to remove the fat on it<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">If Rav Ḥisda inferred his interpretation of R. Jehudah’s position from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 3:7:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.3.7.1">Mishnah 3:7</a>, his argument has to be rejected since Samuel explained it as action necessary for the actual preparation of food, not a preparatory one. Since practice does not follow R. Jehudah, no conclusive answer is needed.</i>.
May one light an idle candle<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">A candle lit for no particular purpose.</i>? Ḥizqiah said, it is forbidden. A <i>baraita</i> disagreed with Ḥizqiah: “<i>Do not make fire in all of your dwelling places on Sabbath day</i><sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 35:3" href="/Exodus.35.3"><i>Ex.</i> 35:3</a>.</i>. On the Sabbath you may not make fire, but you make fire on a holiday.<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">The last <i>baraita</i> in <i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael.</i></i>” If you would say, we deal with cases connected with food, is there not written, <i>only what can be eaten by any breathing being, that alone may be made by you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 12:16" href="/Exodus.12.16"><i>Ex.</i> 12:16</a>.</i>. Therefore what we are dealing with an idle candle<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The argument goes as follows. From the verse quoted first we infer that making a fire is forbidden only on the Sabbath, therefore not on the holiday. The verse quoted second implies that one has to cook, and therefore make fire, on a holiday. If the permission to make fire were restricted to the preparation of food, the inference from the first verse would not be needed. Therefore the permission to make fire extends to fire not needed for the preparation of food; e. g., for lighting. This still does not cover permission for candles lit for no particular purpose.</i>. Rebbi Avuna said, it was stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">The reference is to Mishnai 1:6, where the House of Hillel argue that carrying from a private into the public domain is permitted for any purpose since it is permitted to transport food. Similarly they must argue that making a fire is permitted for any purpose since it is permitted for making food. This still requires an argument that a candle lit for no particular purpose still increases the enjoyment of the holiday.</i>, the House of Shammai forbid but the House of Hillel permit. Rebbi Naḥum the brother of Rebbi Ila asked before Rebbi Joḥanan. He said to him, do neither forbid nor permit<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">One cannot forbid since one follows the teachings of the House of Hillel. One cannot permit since there is no proof that a candle lit for no particular purpose increases the enjoyment of the holiday. (As noted earlier, the permission to make fire does not include permission to generate new fire, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:2:15" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.2.15">Note 85</a>.)</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Animals and vessels are like the feet of their owner<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">On a holiday a person may not leave his Sabbath domain. As on a Sabbath, on a holiday he may make an <i>eruv teḥumim</i> to move his Sabbath domain. Since on a holiday one may carry in the public domain, the <i>eruv</i> extends to all movable property of the person who makes it. That a thing is “like the feet of a person” means that it may be carried to any place accessible to that person but no other place.<br>Note that the grammatical plural בְּעָלִים means a single owner.</i>. If he hands over his animal to his son or to a shepherd they are like his own feet. Vessels particular to one of the brothers in a common household are like his feet, but those not particular are like they place where they walk<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">If some of the members of the household made <i>eruvin</i>, the common vessels can be transported only in a domain accessible to all of them.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> The Mishnah if he handed it over on the holiday; but if he handed it over to him on holiday eve it is like the shepherd’s feet. If there is there one shepherd, but if there is not one shepherd there, like the feet of the cow hand. And it was stated thus: “If he hands his animal to the cow hand even though he did not inform the cow hand it is like the cow hand’s feet.<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">An animal is like the feet of its owner only if the shepherd was not informed before the start of the holiday. This applies if there is a choice of shepherds (that there is at least one other shepherd available to compete for his business) and the owner did not make up his mind before the holiday. But if there is only one cow hand, the owner already knows that if he does not want to slaughter the animal that it will be given to that cow hand, it is as if delivered before the holiday and may be moved only to places accessible to the cow hand. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 37b" href="/Beitzah.37b">Babli 37b</a>.</i>”

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If one borrows vessels from another person, on holiday eve they are like the feet of the borrower, on the holiday like the feet of the lender. If a woman borrowed from another spices, water, and salt, for her dough, they are like the feet of both of them<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">Both the ingredients and the dough may be moved only to a place accessible to both women.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah excludes water since it lacks stability<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Since water may be taken from a river or an aqueduct bringing water from outside the Sabbath domain, the domain restrictions cannot apply to it.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph also is in <i>Ma`aser šeni</i>2:1 (Notes 52–54,<b>ש</b>).</i> Rebbi Abba said, for <i>eruv</i> they went according to the logical rule<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">Since the dough contains contributions from both women, one does not have to try to allocate parts. This is quite obvious here; the argument refers to the difference between the rules of <i>eruv</i> and those of Second Tithe.</i>. You should know that this is so since they say there<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">In Babylonia. In this version the dough can be moved in the common domain even if only the firewood came from a person with a different Sabbath domain. Firewood cannot be bought with Second Tithe money and therefore cannot acquire the holiness of tithe. This shows that the rules of <i>eruv</i> and those of Second Tithe are not comparable.</i> in the name of Rav Ḥisda, but they do not know whether from a tradition or a Mishnah, ‘even logs.’ Did we want to say that logs have no stability?
“Rebbi Jehudah excludes water since it lacks stability.” What is the difference between them<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">The easiest interpretation of this statement presumes that a quote of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Beitzah (Lieberman) 4" href="/Tosefta_Beitzah_(Lieberman).4">Tosephta 4</a>:6 is missing here, “Rebbi Jehudah excludes water since it it is absorbed in the dough” (and therefore not recognizable anymore, nor can it be tasted like spices.) Since we have one statement of R. Jehudah but two reasons given, the question arises whether there are practical implications resulting from the adoption of either the Mishnah’s or the Tosephta’s versions.</i>? Hot water. He who said, because it lacks stability, it has stability<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">Hot water is heated in a pot, it is never flowing (except in hot water springs which are not considered here.)</i>. He who says because they are absorbed in the dough, it is not absorbed in the dish<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">Bread or cake is dry even if the dough absorbed much water; in a cooked dish the water produces sauce and still is visible. The Tosephta implies that a dish cooked with borrowed hot water may be transported only within the domain common to giver and recipient. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 39a" href="/Beitzah.39a">Babli 39a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 97b" href="/Eruvin.97b"><i>Eruvin</i>97b</a>.</i>.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A burning charcoal is like the feet of its owner but a flame may be everywhere<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">A person who made an <i>eruv</i> may light his candle on a fire belonging to another person having made a different <i>eruv</i>. The vessel containing the burning flame still can be moved in the entire Sabbath domain of its owner.</i>. One does not commit larceny with burning charcoals of the Temple; one may not use its flame but one does not commit larceny<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Using anything valuable from the Sanctuary triggers the obligation of a reparation sacrifice and restitution of 125% of the value used (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:15-16" href="/Leviticus.5.15-16"><i>Lev.</i> 5:15–16</a>). Therefore with all other sources of the Mishnah one has to read: “one commits”. But the flame has no monetary value and using it does not require restitution and therefore not a sacrifice. But it still is illicit use and forbidden.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Beitzah (Lieberman) 4:7" href="/Tosefta_Beitzah_(Lieberman).4.7">Tosephta 4:7</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Berakhot 8:6:4" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Berakhot.8.6.4"><i>Berakhot</i>8:7 (Notes 139–144</a>), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 29a" href="/Beitzah.29a">Babli 29a</a>.</i>“Five things were said about burning charcoal and five about the flame. One commits larceny with the burning charcoal of the Temple; one may not use its flame but one cannot commit larceny with the latter<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Using anything valuable from the Sanctuary triggers the obligation of a reparation sacrifice and restitution of 125% of the value used (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 5:15-16" href="/Leviticus.5.15-16"><i>Lev.</i> 5:15–16</a>). Therefore with all other sources of the Mishnah one has to read: “one commits”. But the flame has no monetary value and using it does not require restitution and therefore not a sacrifice. But it still is illicit use and forbidden.</i>. Burning charcoal of idolatry is forbidden, its flame is allowed. He who makes a vow not to use anything of another person may not use his burning charcoal but is allowed his flame. He who carries burning charcoal into the public domain<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">On the Sabbath.</i> is liable<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">For a Sabbath violation. The flame essentially is immaterial; no minimal weight or size can be established for liability.</i> but for the flame he is free of punishment. One makes the benediction<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>havdalah</i> benediction at the end of the Sabbath when fire again can be lit.</i> over the flame but not over glowing charcoal.” Rav Ḥiyya bar Ashi in the name of Rav: If the charcoal was crackling one makes the benediction. Rebbi Joḥanan from Karṣion in the name of Rebbi Naḥum bar Simai: Only if {the flame} is jumping off<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">More or less this is the definition of “crackling”.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> A private cistern is like the feet of the individual, but one of the townspeople is like the feet of the people of this town<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Each town dweller according to his own Sabbath domain.</i>, and of the pilgrims from Babylonia<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">Cisterns established on the route from Babylonia to Jerusalem; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Eruvin 2:1:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Eruvin.2.1.3"><i>Eruvin</i> Chapter 2, Note 24</a>.</i> like the feet of the person filling.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> [A well]<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s text; the scribe’s cannot be read. Probably it was בּוֹר “cistern”, which does not fit the sequel.</i> between two Sabbath domains. Rebbi Joḥanan said, one makes an iron wall for it<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">To separate the waters of the different domains. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Eruvin 48a" href="/Eruvin.48a">Babli <i>Eruvin</i>48a</a>.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina said, even a partition made of reeds<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">A porous symbolic fence used as a token of separation, in the spirit of R. Jehudah (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.4.1">Note 99</a>).</i>, on condition that the water not flow in both directions. Rebbi Yudan said, they were more strict with their words than with words of the Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Since by the argument of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Beitzah 5:4:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Beitzah.5.4.1">Note 99</a> there should be no necessity for a separator of any kind. While rejected in the Yerushalmi, the fact that in certain rabbinic ordinances one is more restrictive than in the interpretation of biblical precepts is accepted in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ketubot 83b" href="/Ketubot.83b">Babli, <i>Ketubot</i>83b</a>.</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina said, is it not {mixture of} kind in its own kind<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Which cannot be disregarded in the most minute amounts, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Terumot 10:6:3" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Terumot.10.6.3"><i>Terumot</i>10:8, Note 107</a>.</i>? But they were strict with their words as with words of the Torah.
This implies that if one finds a vessel on the road it is like the feet of the finder<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the statement that water drawn from a well prepared for the pilgrims from Babylonia acquires the status of the person drawing it.</i>.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If somebody had produce in another village and the people of that village made an <i>eruv</i> to come to him, they should not bring him his produce<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">Since produce has the status of its owner, an <i>eruv</i> made by other people has no influence on his produce, which may not be moved at all if stored outside of his Sabbath domain. But he himself may make an <i>eruv</i> which includes the storage facility of his produce in his Sabbath domain.</i>. But if he made an <i>eruv</i>, his produce has his status.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rav and Samuel: one says, like the feet of the depositor<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">What is the status of things held in deposit for another person on the holiday? The problem is not solved by the Mishnaiot of the Chapter since by depositing the owner renounces temporarily his ability to dispose of the deposit. Since the discussion refers only to the opinion that the holder of the deposit is the one able to move it on the holiday, the Yerushalmi intimates that this is practice to be followed. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 40a" href="/Beitzah.40a">Babli concurs, 40a</a>.</i>. The other one says, they are like the feet of him they are deposited with. The Mishnah disagrees with him who says, they are like the feet of him they are deposited with. As we have stated, “If somebody had produce in another village and the people of that village made an <i>eruv</i> to come to him, they should not bring him his produce” If you would say, they are like the feet of him they are deposited with, they should bring him his produce. Rebbi Yudan said, explain it if the key was in the hands of the owner, or that he did not concede his powers to them before the start of the holiday. And what says this? “If he invited guests they may not carry away their parts unless through another person he gave them the right to their parts on the eve of the holiday”. Are they not like the feet of him they are deposited with from the moment that he gave them the rights to their parts.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If he invited guests<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">Who may reach his place only by making an <i>eruv</i>.</i> they may not carry away their parts unless through another person he gave them the right to their parts on the eve of the holiday<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">He must give them ownership of their parts before the start of the holiday. But ownership of a gift is transferred only by acceptance by the recipient or his representative. On the other hand, one may act to the benefit of another person without the latter’s knowledge. Therefore the person who invites can ask a third party to formally accept the gifts to his guests for them without their knowledge before the start of the holiday.</i>. One does not water or slaughter prairie animals<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">מִדְבָּר is not “desert” but, based on the Aramaic meaning of דבר “to lead”, it is the place where animals are lead to graze, i. e., any place unfit for agriculture.</i> but one waters and slaughters domestic animals. What are domestic animals? Those that stay overnight in the village, prairie animals that stay overnight in the dust.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The following are the prairie animals, those who leave on Passover and return with the rains. The following are the domestic ones, those who stay in the village overnight. Rebbi says, it is permitted to slaughter these and those which entered the Sabbath domain after dark. What are prairie animals? Those who grow up in the dust.<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">Rebbi considers the two categories enumerated in the Mishnah as domestic animals and therefore prepared as food; the only animals not in this category are those who never see a barn but stay outside also in winter.</i>”<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Beitzah (Lieberman) 4:11" href="/Tosefta_Beitzah_(Lieberman).4.11">Tosephta 4:11</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Beitzah 40a" href="/Beitzah.40a">Babli 40a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 45b" href="/Shabbat.45b"><i>Šabbat</i>45b</a>.</i> Rebbi Ze`ira said, this implies, it is permitted to move a vessel which entered the Sabbath domain from outside the Sabbath domain. Rebbi Simeon bar Karsana in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: But only within four cubits<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">While there is no problem with <i>muqṣeh</i> according to R. Ze`irah, there still remains the rule that persons and things having been outside a Sabbath domain any time during Sabbath or holiday, upon (re-)entry may move or be moved only within 4 cubits. This rule is not waived.</i>. As this, a Saracen honored Gamliel the Twin with truffles<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">On a holiday, and truffles are not found in town.</i>. He came and asked Rebbi Mana who said to him, receive them in your kitchen<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Greek μαγειρεῑον.</i> and eat them within four cubits.
